< review>
They slay at nail art. This is my 3rd time going, and I swear they get better every single time. I'm an introvert who hates socializing. I go in, just show the lady what I want and she does it. They tell you the price before they start. Every nail station is busy, so make an appointment or go when you have free time. I like short and simple nails, but the ladies there never try to sell me on long fancy nails, which I love. It took about an hour but you could tell they she wanted it perfect. < review>
This review is for Stallion Springs (Tehachapi), CA

I'm active duty military so I've moved around quite a bit.  Race internet is the fastest connection for the lowest price you can find in the country right now.  Gigabit fiber for $60/month.  According to AT&Ts CEO, that's economically impossible, but Race seems to be doing just fine.
The only two complaints I have are that you'll have to wait on hold a while if you need customer service (though not nearly as long as most other telecoms I've dealt with, and you'll get someone in the US that speaks english natively) and you can't report an outage if you aren't on the account (we ran into this problem while housesitting at my in-laws).

Note:  some of the other reviews say that they don't get the full advertised speed with this service.  If you're using WiFi, you will never see full gigabit speeds unless you have a WiFi 6 access point and you have line of sight to the antenna.  For most AC access points you should expect 200-300 Mbps under real world conditions.  If you want to see the full speed you need to be connected with a wired connection.< /review>

The woman who wrote the long tirade (Kelly) which all seemed to be one sentence, included such eloquent proclamations as: 'that was wrong in the wrong I don't do drugs no more that is poison...' is clearly insane.  The other couple who complained about the homeless ('indigent') population being seen before her and her husband, I would say: Firstly, who calls homeless people 'indigents' anymore (or ever)?  We're not living in the colonial deep South....  Secondly, Eureka has an extremely high homeless population.  I would say it's an indication of how GOOD the hospital is that it triaged the homeless patients quickly, instead of leaving them there waiting for hours.  Just because you're not homeless doesn't mean you get to be bumped up the Triage levels.  Last I checked, being middle-class wasn't a medical emergency...  All the other reviews seemed to be written by people who have never been into an Emergency Room before - yes, you have to wait, it's called a 'Triage' system.  Search it up.  If you don't like it, blame the French - they invented it.  If you don't like waiting for medical care I suggest you tell Obama, he made it available for everyone regardless of ability to pay.  I suggest you try working on the other side of the fence and see what health care providers have to deal with on a day-to-day basis before you start bitching about your 3-hour wait for a hang nail....
Good job Eureka!  You're a rural hospital with a high homeless population doing the best you can.  Forget the negative Nancy's.  I commend you.</Review>

<Review>After several months of research, I had decided on the Chevy Bolt as my new chariot. The next step was to find a dealership. There are a handful in the area, but Connell Chevrolet had the highest rating at 4.5 stars out of 5. They also had the most Bolts in their inventory at different price ranges. This lead me to believe that they had carefully curated this assortment to be able to showcase the car and its capabilities. Other dealerships in the area only had one or two Bolts in their inventory; which leads me to think that they may not care to keep these vehicles stocked and that maybe the sales force would not be as familiar with the car. As I scan through the glowing reviews, one name showed up several times: TIM CONNELL. There's my guy. I'd rather not waste time and effort dealing with any potential rookie sales people. Been there, done that. So I went to Connell Chevrolet dealership on a Sunday and asked for Tim. No problem at all. No one tried to swipe me as a client with that 'oh I can help you instead' line. And that tells me a lot about the integrity of the staff at this dealership. There are old business cards framed on the wall from the lineage of Connell men over the last several decades. This family business prides itself on good customer service, not only at time of purchase, but also after the fact. Anyway, I was lead directly to Tim Connell. Tim is very friendly and personable. We spent a couple hours reviewing the cars in the inventory (which was 3 more cars than what showed up in the online inventory), test driving, reviewed all the optional packages, looked at comparison charts, inventory from other dealerships, appraised my trade-in vehicle, prices and incentives. Tim was very patient while I weighed my options. And ultimately, he helped me find the perfect Bolt at another dealership and would have it transferred post haste. < review>
Used car shopping is pretty much a terrible time. I called Connell because I saw a used van on their lot I was interested in. Tim walked out to the car while on the phone and checked the condition for me (it was about a 45 minute drive for us).

Everything looked ok so we made the trip down there that night. As I said in the beginning, I hate car shopping, so I make sure I have literally everything in order. I had my own financing in order from Bank of America (I did some research first and found their rates the most competitive - plus it's my main bank).

When we got to the dealership, Tim just handed us the keys, didn't ask for license or anything. Didn't even sit with us during the test drive. I liked this approach. I find the salesperson standing over me to be more of a nuisance. He was readily available if we had any questions.

When we got to the purchase part of the entertainment, Tim asked how we were going to pay. I told him we were financing it and I gave Tim my pre-approval from Bank of America. In order to get the pre-approval, BoA obviously had to run my credit. Tim said he thought it was a good rate but thought they might be able to beat it. I told Tim I was ONLY interested in them running my credit AGAIN if the finance manager was positive he could beat the rate. I said this probably 5 times - I am very conscious about my credit.

He agreed and left for probably 15 minutes. When he came back, he told me that his finance manager ran my credit and got me a Bank of America loan! "Congratulations! This way it'll be easier than using the pre-approval process". I was visibly annoyed at this. I had already done my research and knew BoA was the best rate at the time. They went directly against my request and ran my credit anyways. Pretty sure the dealer gets an incentive for every loan they originate and I'm also pretty sure they willfully ignored my request to not re-run my credit if they couldn't beat the rate.

Then Tim said the van only had 1 key. They would have a 2nd key made. Since we live about 45 minutes away, Tim assured us that his guy could drive out to where we live to make us the new key. About a week after the purchase, we find that his guy couldn't make us the key, and we'd need to bring it to a local dealer to have the key made. Tim agreed to pay us $200 (no more) to have the key made at the local dealer. Of course, keys these days are nearly $300 to have programmed. So we were out almost $100 in the ordeal.

Long story short, it was a decent experience. Tim was nice. There were a couple things that made the experience a 4-star rather than 5, but at the end of the day, it wasn't terrible. I'd buy from them again.<//review>

Side note: It had a complete top to bottom crack down the middle of the windshield that "the dealer was unaware of."  I'm not sad about the loss of that deal, though. I love my Prius for its supreme fuel efficiency and completely equipped dash system including backup assistance, satellite navigation, satellite radio, and Bluetooth sync options. I would have sacrificed all the things I love about my current vehicle for more uphill horsepower and the ability to attach a bike/surf rack, which I believe I can still do, with some modifications. So, the only thing my hybrid needs is more horsepower...hint hint to any engineer reading this.  Nonetheless, my experience at Connell was average. The lot was clean and organized like any other, but I was handed off to a couple of sales guys before the final guy entertained the idea of dealing with me. I don't think I was overbearing. I simply had a firm handshake and let them know it was not my first rodeo dealing with cars on any level. I was provided a lot of excuses " I don't know a lot about your car of interest" which made me feel like they didn't care about the products they were selling or whether I bought the car or not. I let them know that I wanted to learn more about the Jeep, as I had never owned one, but there was not any excitement to share with me about it or any of the new Chevy products. Granted, it was 8:30 PM. The staff was obviously tired. Which leads me to the question of why the owner of the lot extended his hours to such an absurd time. I don't think sales professionals selling high dollar products should be required to work past 6 or 7 pm unless they desire to assist or accommodate preferred clients. An American brand not promoting implied family values by keeping their employees late? Preposterous!   For Pete's sake, they are not teenagers at the mall closing down a dress shop. If you want to make your lot stand out from the others, start doing what others are not doing. Create an experience. Make the buyer, no matter the price point, feel important. Instill pride in your system and your sales people so that your beloved patrons are proud to initiate and repeat business with you. Quit being so gosh darn greedy by exploiting your employees time, talent, and resources. Know their dreams. Help build them up. By the way, the guy I dealt with is freelance IT guy with a computer science degree of some sort itching to leverage into something more aligned with who he is...would he be better suited in the service department, running computer analytics in the garage, or dealing more on the internet side of the business? <review>I bought a new Colorado from Connell two weeks ago.
I 'negotiated' a price with the salesman on the phone prior, and because I had just sold my Jeep I had someone give me a ride to Connell to pick the truck up. This was a mistake. The price escalated by about $1500 when I got to the finance office, and instead of there being just one rebate, there ended up being two. When I asked the finance woman about it, she claimed ignorance. When I asked her to show me the figure on the contract that showed the 'net' price, she claimed she didn't understand the contract well enough to know what that was.
Anyway, I'm a big boy. I could've stood up and walked out,  I didn't because it would've been a LONG walk since I didn't have a vehicle-which is prolly why they 'tweaked' the figures on me. Oh well, you live, you learn.

On the drive home I couldn't figure out how to get some features on the radio working(the salesman apparently was too busy to go over the truck with me) so I called Chv customer service. I was told that I needed to download a couple apps first so I did. When I couldn't sign into said apps, I called back. This time I was told that I first needed to create an account on some website, so I shelved this.
The next day while driving the truck for the second time it went into 'Limp Mode'.
It took me almost two hours to get the 15 miles home, as it would only rev to 2,000rpm, thus would only do 10-15mph. Onstar told me to drive it home but to 'avoid large hills'(I happen to live on a large hill).
So when I got home I called Chv roadside assistance(this was a Sunday) to have the truck towed back to the dealer. After two hours of them not being able to get a tow truck , I called AAA. It was getting late and the dealer was gonna close.
The next day when I spoke with the service writer, he told me an electrical connection wasn't plugged in correctly at the factory, so they fixed it and told me to come get it.
On my way home I stopped to show some friends my new truck. They pointed out that the coolant reservoir was COMPLETELY EMPTY, so I bought some coolant and filled it up. I took a pic of it to show Connell, and decided it would be a good idea to stop in and have them check all the fluids. A couple days later I did just that, and they sent it to the back to be checked.
So when that was done I left. A few miles out a bird pooped on my windshield so I hit the washer button. When the washer didn't work, I spun around and went back to Connell. The service writer opened the hood, and low and behold the washer reservoir was also totally empty.
When I was talking to the service writer I mentioned the problems I was having with the radio. He took me inside and introduced me to Mike Erickson-the product specialist. Although he was clearly busy, he stopped what he was doing and went with me out to my vehicle, where he went over everything on it, and stayed with me until I clearly understood everything.
I am very thankful MIke Burroughs(the service writer) took the time to introduce me to Mike Erickson, and very thankful Mike Erickson took the time to thoroughly go over my vehicle with me, and stay with me 'til I was done with my questions.
If it weren't for the two Mikes, I'd probably have called Chevy to complain about the horrible experience I had purchasing this truck, but they turned my experience around.
I'm still not happy about paying more than what we agreed upon, but again, I could've walked out at any time. I'm also not happy about them not doing the PDI properly on my truck, which cost me several hours when it was all said and done.
I'm giving them 3 stars, and it would've been ZERO if not for the two MIkes.
If you buy a vehicle from Connell, I STRONGLY suggest you find MIke Erickson to show you your new vehicle, then introduce yourself to Mike Burroughs in the service dept.</review><pics>None< /pics>< Response>
